#  About
The Department of Revenue is Washington state’s primary tax agency, nationally recognized for innovation and quality customer service. Revenue administers about 60 categories of taxes that help fund education, social services, health care, corrections, public safety, natural resource conservation, and other important services counted on by Washington residents. Find out more about [what we do](https://dor.wa.gov/about/what-we-do).
![Blue icon with three heads](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/styles/thumbnail/public/2023-09/Whoweare.png?itok=eB09763Z&uid=69a0c7a758f56)

## **Read about it**

[Agency Strategic Business Plan 2024-2029](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2025-01/StrategicBusinessPlan-2024.pdf) (PDF)
## Vision
Achieve the highest level of voluntary compliance by being the trusted leader in tax administration and  
public service.
## Mission
To efficiently administer tax laws and public service programs with integrity.
## Goals
**Workforce management**  
We attract and develop the best teams.
**Tax & program administration**  
Simplify, educate and enforce.
**Customer experience**  
Build relationships. Empower success.
**Promote innovation**  
Ideas creating value.
## Values - I CARE
Integrity  
Cooperation  
Accountability  
Respect  
Excellence
## Foundation
Sound tax and operational policy  
Everyday leadership  
Engaged employees  
Integrated performance management  
Leveraging technology

#  Your privacy
## [Agency privacy notice](https://dor.wa.gov/contact/your-privacy/agency-privacy-notice)
Comprehensive notice that explains how an agency collects, uses, shares, and manages personal information.
## [Website privacy notice](https://dor.wa.gov/contact/your-privacy/website-privacy-notice)
Limited notice that explains what information is collected when you visit a website, and how that information is used, shared, and managed.

#  Public records
The Department of Revenue is subject to the Washington Public Records Act, [Chapter 42.56](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/rcw/default.aspx?cite=42.56&full=true) RCW. Many public records are available on the Revenue Website at the following links:
For information on | Go to  
---|---  
**For information on** A specific business |  **Go to** [Business lookup](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/gteunauth/?Link=Lookup)  
**For information on** Business licenses and endorsements |  **Go to** [Business lookup](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/gteunauth/?Link=Lookup)  
**For information on** Open data on tax collections, forecasts, statistics, reports, and studies |  **Go to** [Get statistics and reports](https://dor.wa.gov/about/statistics-reports)  
**For information on** Tax incentives and preferences: surveys and reports |  **Go to** [Public disclosure reports](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/gteunauth/_/#2)  
**For information on** Unclaimed property |  **Go to** [ClaimYourCash.org](http://ucp.dor.wa.gov/)  
**For information on** Revenue forms and publications |  **Go to** [Get a form or publication](https://dor.wa.gov/forms-publications)  
**For information on** Rule-making process, advisories, decisions and opinions |  **Go to** [Public records index-rule making and final opinions](https://dor.wa.gov/contact/e-mail/public-records-index-rule-making-and-final-opinions)  
**For information on** Online tax research tool including DOR and state laws, rules and tax documents |  **Go to** [Taxpedia](http://taxpedia.dor.wa.gov/)  
**For information on** Other public records |  **Go to** [Public records index](https://dor.wa.gov/public-records-index)  
## Releasing confidential customer information
Much of the information collected and held by the Department of Revenue for its customers is confidential and exempt from the Public Records Act. Various laws restrict access to taxpayer and business information and exempt these records from the Public Records Act, including:
[RCW 82.32.330: Taxpayer Information](http://app.leg.wa.gov/rcw/default.aspx?cite=82.32.330)
[RCW 19.02.115: Licensing Information](http://app.leg.wa.gov/rcw/default.aspx?cite=19.02.115)
[RCW 84.08.210: Property Tax Information](http://app.leg.wa.gov/rcw/default.aspx?cite=84.08.210)
[RCW 63.30.820: Unclaimed Property Confidential Information](https://app.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=63.30.820)
Public information is available on the Revenue website, related to the sites above. To obtain confidential information about a specific taxpayer or business, use the following forms:
  * Taxpayer information: [Confidential Tax Information Authorization](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/42-2446e.pdf)
  * Licensing information: [Confidential Licensing Information Authorization](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/700002.pdf)
  * Unclaimed Property information: [Confidential Unclaimed Property Information Authorization](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2026-02/80-0061.pdf)


Other public records forms:
The law prohibits the Department of Revenue from releasing lists of individuals or taxpayers to requestors if the request is made for a commercial purpose. You must submit the following form and describe the purpose of your request:
Lists of licenses, individuals, and/or taxpayers: [Declaration of Non-Commercial Purpose​](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/ComPurpIndividuals.pdf)
## Subpoenas or Court Orders
Submit subpoenas or court orders to the Department of Revenue, Information Governance Office or to dorpublicrecords@dor.wa.gov.
[More Information](https://dor.wa.gov/contact/public-records#more-info-collapse-block)
## How to submit a public records request
To request a public record, we recommend you use our online [Public Records Request Center](https://DORWA.GOVQA.US/WEBAPP/_RS/SUPPORTHOME.ASPX), where you can communicate with our public records unit about your request and download your records directly when they are ready.
When making your request, please identify and describe in detail the records you are requesting. Please include the subject matter, date range, types of records requested and appropriate divisions or programs. Failure to provide sufficient information to locate the records you request may cause delay.
Please include any required attachments, which may include the [Confidential Tax Information Authorization](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/42-2446e.pdf) (CTIA), [Confidential Licensing Information Authorization](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/700002.pdf) (CLIA), [Confidential Unclaimed Property Information Authorization](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2026-02/80-0061.pdf) (CUPIA) or the [Declaration for Non-Commercial Purpose](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/ComPurpIndividuals.pdf).
### [Submit a request](https://DORWA.GOVQA.US/WEBAPP/_RS/SUPPORTHOME.ASPX)
### Charges for copies
The Department of Revenue may charge for copies of public records. We may also charge an additional cost for compiling customized lists and data. Please see the [statement of costs](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/DORCosts_for_Public_Records_Requests.pdf) for more information.
###  [​​](https://DORWA.GOVQA.US/WEBAPP/_RS/SUPPORTHOME.ASPX)For questions, contact us:
Department of Revenue   
Public Records, Information Governance Office   
​PO Box 47456  
Olympia, WA 98504-7456  
DORPublicRecords@dor.wa.gov  
Phone: [360-704-5741](tel:360-704-5741)  
Fax: [360-534-1606](tel:360-534-1606)

Print
#  Report no business activity
[Leer este contenido en español.](https://dor.wa.gov/informacion-en-espanol/guias/declarar-ausencia-actividad-comercial)
## Report online
You have two options to report no business activity electronically:
  * [**Express file** online](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/gteunauth/_/?Link=ExpressNoBusiness).
  * **E-file** a “no business” return online using our tax filing system, [My DOR](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/home/). Simply log into [My DOR](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/home/). You will need to have [access to your tax account](https://dor.wa.gov/manage-business/my-dor-help/set).


## Report by phone
  1. Call 360-705-6705.
  2. At the greeting, enter "111."
  3. Enter your 9-digit Account ID (found on your tax return, above your name and address).
  4. Follow the instructions given.


When you file by phone, you do not need to mail us your paper return.
[More Information](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/report-no-business-activity#more-info-collapse-block)

#  Filing frequencies & due dates
## Filing frequencies
After you registered your business, we sent you a packet of information. In this packet there is a welcome letter with your:
  * Account ID
  * Filing frequency (monthly, quarterly, annual)


Filing frequencies are assigned based on what you estimate for your yearly business income. See the table below for annual, quarterly, and monthly details. For additional information, please see WAC 458-20-22801 on [Tax reporting frequency](https://apps.leg.wa.gov/wac/default.aspx?cite=458-20-22801). You can request an update to your excise tax account filing frequency by calling our call center at [360-705-6705](tel:360-705-6705).
### Filing frequencies based on annual tax liability
Frequency | Annual Tax Liability  
---|---  
**Frequency** Annual |  **Annual Tax Liability** Annual tax liability  
$1,050 or less  
**Frequency** Quarterly |  **Annual Tax Liability** Annual tax liability  
$1,051 - $4,800  
**Frequency** Monthly |  **Annual Tax Liability** Annual tax liability  
$4,801 - greater  
###  Filing frequencies based on estimated gross annual income in Washington
Business activities | Annual | Quarterly | Monthly  
---|---|---|---  
**Business activities** Retail |  **Annual** $0 - $60,000 |  **Quarterly** $60,000 - $100,000 |  **Monthly** $60,000 +  
**Business activities** Service |  **Annual** $0 - $60,000 |  **Quarterly** $60,000 - $100,000 |  **Monthly** $60,000 +  
**Business activities** Manufacturing |  **Annual** $0 - $60,000 |  **Quarterly** $60,000 - $100,000 |  **Monthly** $60,000 +  
**Business activities** Wholesale |  **Annual** $0 - $60,000 |  **Quarterly** $60,000 - $100,000 |  **Monthly** $60,000 +  
### Filing frequencies for specialized activities based on income range
Business activity | Annual | Quarterly | Monthly  
---|---|---|---  
**Business activity** Construction |  **Annual** N/A |  **Quarterly** $0 - $60,000 |  **Monthly** $60,000 +  
**Business activity** Restaurant |  **Annual** N/A |  **Quarterly** $0 - $60,000 |  **Monthly** $60,000 +  
**Business activity** Auto Dealers |  **Annual** N/A |  **Quarterly** $0 - $100,000 |  **Monthly** $0 - $100,000  
**Business activity** Truck drivers |  **Annual** $0 - $60,000 |  **Quarterly** $60,000 + |  **Monthly** N/A  
## [Due dates](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/filing-frequencies-due-dates/filing-due-dates)
  * Monthly returns are due the 25th of every month. (e.g. The June tax return is due July 25.)
  * Quarterly returns are due the end of the month following the tax quarter. (e.g. The Quarter 1 (Jan, Feb, Mar) tax return is due April 30.)
  * Annual returns are due April 15. (e.g. The Annual 2019 tax return is due April 15, 2020)


If the due date falls on a [weekend or legal holiday](https://dor.wa.gov/contact/state-holiday-schedule), the due date is extended to the next business day.
## [Annual business filers](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/filing-frequencies-due-dates/annual-business-filers)
For your convenience, we’ve compiled all of the helpful information, links, and resources that you’ll need to complete your annual tax return.
## [Active nonreporters ](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/filing-frequencies-due-dates/active-non-reporting)
Businesses that meet certain criteria may be eligible for active non-reporting status. Active non-reporting status means you are actively doing business in Washington, but you are not required to file tax returns. To qualify, your business must meet all the following criteria:
  * Business activity does not require the collection of [retail sales tax](https://dor.wa.gov/find-taxes-rates/retail-sales-tax).
  * For calendar years starting Jan. 1, 2023, or later, gross proceeds of sales, gross income, or value of products for all [business and occupation (B&O) tax classifications](https://dor.wa.gov/open-business/apply-business-license/plan-taxes/business-and-occupation-bo-tax-classification-definitions) is less than $125,000 per year.
  * For calendar years before January 1, 2023, gross proceeds of sales, gross income, or value of products for all business and occupation (B&O) tax classifications is less than $28,000 per year; or $46,667 per year for persons generating at least 50% of their income from activities taxable under RCW 82.04.255, 82.04.290(2)(a), and 82.04.285.
  * Gross income of the business for all [public utility tax (PUT) classifications](https://dor.wa.gov/open-business/apply-business-license/plan-taxes/state-public-utility-and-other-tax-classification-definitions) is less than $24,000 per year.
  * The business does not owe any [other tax or fee](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/other-taxes) to the Department of Revenue.


[More Information](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/filing-frequencies-due-dates#more-info-collapse-block)

#  Careers
[ ![Watch a video: Why work at Revenue](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2024-04/Recruit_splash.png?uid=69a0c90909d51) ](https://iframe.dacast.com/vod/b280e90764fc353782d89dd6cba9d80b/52243845-d53c-28f7-d903-9c90abb649c6)
  
[Watch a video: Why work at Revenue (2:13)](https://iframe.dacast.com/vod/b280e90764fc353782d89dd6cba9d80b/52243845-d53c-28f7-d903-9c90abb649c6)
[Search for jobs](https://www.governmentjobs.com/careers/washington?department%5B0%5D=Dept.%20of%20Revenue&sort=PostingDate%7CDescending)
![Blue circle with white icon of a star over three vertical bars, to symbolize first place.](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/styles/thumbnail/public/2023-07/CareersIcon-StarGraph.png?itok=hR7NIil9&uid=69a0c9091197a)
91% of Revenue employees say, "My supervisor treats me with respect."[1](https://dor.wa.gov/about/careers#fn1)
![Universal access icon: blue circle behind white human figure with arms and legs outstretched.](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/styles/thumbnail/public/2023-07/CareersIcon-UniversalAccess.png?itok=01HNCyhP&uid=69a0c90917945)
Of our new hires:
  * 6% identify as disabled
  * 42% as a person of color
  * 14% veterans.[2](https://dor.wa.gov/about/careers#fn2)


![Blue circle behind white icon of a ladder, symbolizing career growth.](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/styles/thumbnail/public/2023-07/CareersIcon-Ladder.png?itok=CLF3WL10&uid=69a0c9091e124)
Around 50% of our job openings are filled as promotions.
## Flexible schedules and telework
Maintain a healthy work-life balance through flexible schedules and workplace arrangements, such as telework and remote fieldwork.
[What employees say about working at Revenue](https://dor.wa.gov/about/careers/what-employees-say-about-revenue).
## Start or grow your career at Revenue
Many rewarding positions are available at Revenue, from forestry to customer service. Plus, advancement opportunities are around every corner—we offer career paths for those who want to do more. 
[Jobs to get you started](https://dor.wa.gov/about/careers/jobs-get-you-started).
## You’re taken care of
Benefits that ensure you’ll have the support you and your family need:
  * [Benefits](http://www.careers.wa.gov/working.html)
  * [Comprehensive healthcare](https://www.hca.wa.gov/employee-retiree-benefits/public-employees)
  * [Deferred compensation](https://www.drs.wa.gov/plan/dcp/)
  * [Dependent Care Assistance Program](https://www.hca.wa.gov/employee-retiree-benefits/public-employees/dependent-care-assistance-program-dcap)
  * [Employee Assistance Program](https://des.wa.gov/services/employee-assistance-program)
  * [Paid Family and Medical Leave](https://paidleave.wa.gov/)
  * [Retirement plans](http://www.drs.wa.gov/)
  * [Tuition reimbursement](https://ofm.wa.gov/state-human-resources/compensation-job-classes/compensation-administration/special-employee-programs)


## Invest in your future
  * Train for certifications like Lean continuous improvement.
  * Grow through mentorship and career paths.
  * Continue learning with tuition reimbursement.


## Safe, accessible, and diverse
Find community at work. Join our employee-led Inclusion, Diversity, and Equity Committee, Veteran Employment Team, or other Employee Resource Groups. Explore the [statewide Business Resource Groups](https://ofm.wa.gov/state-human-resources/workforce-diversity-equity-and-inclusion/statewide-business-resource-groups) for more inclusion opportunities.
## Why Washington
  * Our temperate climate allows for year-round outdoor adventures. Visit our [3 national parks](https://www.nps.gov/state/wa/index.htm), and [170+ state parks](https://parks.wa.gov/). 
  * History and culture abound thanks to [the many tribes who call this place home](https://www.washingtontribes.org/the-tribes-of-washington/). Fans of art and music will appreciate our thriving creative scene.
  * Consistently a top-ranked state to live in, with high marks for fiscal stability, natural environment, infrastructure, and education.
  * Learn about the regions where Revenue offers remote and fieldwork options: [Work where you live](https://dor.wa.gov/about/careers/work-where-you-live).


## Need help or accommodations?
Call Human Resources at [360-704-5731](tel:360-704-5731). TTY, dial [711](tel:711) or [1-800-833-6388](tel:1-800-833-6388). Email us at Jobs@dor.wa.gov.
We embrace diversity and offer a respectful, inclusive culture for all. We encourage people with disabilities, veterans, people over 40, people of any sexual orientation and gender identity, people of all faith or no faith backgrounds, marginalized groups, and people of every ethnic and cultural background to apply. We are an equal-opportunity employer.

Print
#  File or amend my return
## [File online](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/home/)
File your return electronically using My DOR. Simply [log in to My DOR](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/home/) using your Secure Access Washington (SAW) user ID. You will need your tax account ID and letter ID, printed on correspondence from the Department, to sign up.
## File by mail
Starting with your 2020 tax return, you must file and pay electronically. If you haven’t already, please [sign up for My DOR](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/home/Login) and start e-filing your returns.
If you have received a waiver from the department to file by paper, please use the paper return sent to you by mail or download the [form and instructions](https://dor.wa.gov/forms-publications/forms-subject/excise-tax-returns-and-addendums). [Learn more about requesting a waiver](https://dor.wa.gov/forms-publications/publications-subject/tax-topics/all-businesses-are-required-file-and-pay-electronically).
## [Amend my return](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/file-or-amend-my-return/amend-my-return)
If you discover that you made a mistake on a previously filed tax return, you can amend your return. You may go back four years, plus the current year.
## [Payment methods](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/file-or-amend-my-return/payment-methods)
Depending on whether you file your return electronically or by mail, the Department offers several types of payment methods.
## [Self-service payment plan](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/file-or-amend-my-return/self-service-payment-plans-qualifications)
You may qualify for a self-service payment plan for a billed tax liability. Choose from 3, 6, 9, or 12 month payment terms.
[More Information](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/file-or-amend-my-return#more-info-collapse-block)
## More information
[All businesses are required to file and pay electronically](https://dor.wa.gov/forms-publications/publications-subject/tax-topics/all-businesses-are-required-file-and-pay-electronically)
[Information on electronic filing for tax preparers](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/file-or-amend-my-return/information-electronic-filing-tax-preparers)
[Instructions for completing my Combined Excise Tax Return](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/file-or-amend-my-return/instructions-completing-combined-excise-tax-return)
[Capital Gains My DOR help](https://dor.wa.gov/manage-business/my-dor-help/capital-gains-my-dor-help)

#  Late filing
[Don't miss your due date! Sign up for text or email filing reminders.](https://public.govdelivery.com/accounts/WADOR/signup/19970)
## [Excise tax return extensions](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/late-filing/excise-tax-return-extensions)
Depending on the circumstances, the department may grant extensions for filing an excise tax return. The request must be made before the due date.
## [Penalty waivers](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/late-filing/penalty-waivers)
The department can waive late return penalties under certain circumstances. If your return or payment is late and you feel you have a qualifying situation, you may request to have the penalty waived.
## [Delinquent tax collection process](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/late-filing/delinquent-tax-collection-process)
An account becomes delinquent when the due date for a tax return or other established liability has passed and the amount due remains unpaid.
## [Interest rates](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/late-filing/interest-rate-tables)
The interest rates for excise tax assessments and refunds change every year. Access tax interest rate tables for excise tax, estate tax, and REET for current and past years.
[More Information](https://dor.wa.gov/file-pay-taxes/late-filing#more-info-collapse-block)

Print
#  Tax incentives
## [Tax incentive programs](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/incentive-programs)
There are over 50 tax incentive programs available for businesses. These incentives are to encourage the creation and preservation of family-wage jobs, especially in areas with high unemployment.
## [Deductions](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/deductions)
Find out which deductions apply to your business.
## [Credits](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits)
Depending on your business activity, you may qualify for a tax credit.
## [Sales and use tax deferral programs](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/sales-and-use-tax-deferral-programs)
Businesses engaged in manufacturing and other specified activities may be eligible to apply for a sales and use tax deferral.
## [Tax incentive public disclosure reports](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/gteunauth/?Link=IncRpt)
Public disclosure reports that provide tax incentive information reported by businesses, as required by law.
## Get involved
Every year, Washington state reviews its tax preferences on a ten-year schedule, developed by the Citizen Commission for Performance Measurement of Tax Preferences (RCW 43.136).
If you wish to provide testimony, view reports, or learn more about this process, visit [Citizen Commission for Performance Measurement of Tax Preferences](https://leg.wa.gov/about-the-legislature/committees/joint/citizen-commission-for-performance-measurement-of-tax-preferences/).
[More Information](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives#more-info-collapse-block)
## More information
[Tax incentive special notices](https://dor.wa.gov/forms-publications/publications-subject/special-notices)
[List of retail sales and use tax exemptions](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/retail-sales-tax/retail-sales-and-use-tax-exemptions)
[Tax incentive reports & studies](https://dor.wa.gov/about/statistics-reports)

#  Credits
We listed each tax credit definition below. If you need help determining the proper credit, [contact us](https://dor.wa.gov/contact).
**Note:** The number inside the brackets [ ] corresponds to the credit ID number located on your excise tax return. This number is next to each credit definition.
  * [Aerospace Manufacturer B&O Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Aerospace)
  * [Aluminum Smelter Credits](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Aluminum)
  * [Bad Debt Tax Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#BadDebt)
  * [Capital Gains B&O Tax Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#CapGains)
  * [Clean Alternative Fuel Commercial Vehicle and Vehicle Infrastructure Tax Credit ](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#CleanAltFuel)
  * [Commute Trip Reduction Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Commute)
  * [Customized Employee Workforce Training Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Customized)
  * [Destination Sourcing Tax Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Destination)
  * [Employee Ownership Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#EmployeeOwnership)
  * [Energy Efficiency Incentive Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#EnergyEfficiency)
  * [Equitable Access to Credit Program B&O Tax Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#EquitableAccess)
  * [External Multiple Activities Credits (MATC) – Taxes Paid to Other States](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#ExternalMATC)
  * [Hazardous Substance Tax](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Hazardous)
  * [International Services Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#International)
  * [Low-Income Community Solar Project Cost Recovery Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Solar)
  * [Main Street Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Main)


  * [Manufactured/Sold Inside Washington MATC](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#ManufacturedMATC)
  * [Motion Picture Competitiveness Program Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Motion)
  * [Multiple Activities Tax Credit (MATC)](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#MATC)
  * [New Employees in Manufacturing and Research & Development in Rural Counties B&O Tax Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#NewEmployees)
  * [Other Credits](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#OtherCredits)
  * [Pollution Control Credits](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Pollutioncontrol)
  * [Public Utility Tax Credit for Billing Discounts/Qualifying Contributions to a Low Income Home Energy Assistance Fund](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#PUTBillAsst)
  * [Renewable Energy System Cost Recovery Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Recovery)
  * [Sales Tax Paid in Other States](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#OtherStates)
  * [Silicon Smelter Credits](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Silicon)
  * [Small Business B&O Tax Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#SBC)
  * [Syrup Tax Paid B&O Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Syrup)
  * [Tobacco Products/Cigar Tax Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Tobacco)
  * [Vapor Products Credit, All Other](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#VaporProducts)
  * [Vapor Solution Credit, Accessible Containers Greater than 5 mL Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#VaporSolution)
  * [Veterans Employer B&O Tax Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Vet-BNO)
  * [Veterans Employer PUT Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/credits#Vet-PUT)


* * *
##  Aerospace Credits
A business and occupation (B&O) tax credit available to:
  1. [920]  
Manufacturers and processors for hire of commercial airplanes, component parts of commercial airplanes, or aerospace tooling for qualified preproduction development expenditures. An Annual Tax Performance Report must be filed by May 31 of each year after a year when a credit is taken. Electronic filing required.
  2. [910]  
Manufacturers of commercial airplanes, component parts of commercial airplanes, or aerospace tooling equal to property/leasehold excise taxes paid on new buildings, land, and the increased value of renovated buildings used exclusively for manufacturing commercial airplanes, component parts of commercial airplanes, or aerospace tooling and property taxes paid on equipment eligible for the manufacturing machinery and equipment (M&E) exemption. Aerospace non-manufacturers equal to property/leasehold excise taxes paid on new buildings, land, and the increased value of renovated buildings used exclusively in aerospace product development or in providing aerospace services and property taxes on qualifying computer equipment and peripherals used primarily in aerospace product development or in providing aerospace services. Credit can only be taken after property taxes have been paid. An Annual Tax Performance Report must be filed by May 31 of each year after a year when a credit is taken. Electronic filing required.
  3. [935]  
Aerospace Non-Manufacturers. Persons who develop, design, and engineer, but do not manufacture commercial airplanes and component parts thereof are eligible for a B&O tax credit for qualified preproduction development expenditures. The credit must be taken against taxes due for the same calendar year in which the qualified preproduction development expenditures are incurred. An Annual Tax Performance Report must be filed by May 31 of each year after a year when a credit is taken. Electronic filing required.


[Aerospace Industry Incentives](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/tax-incentive-programs)
* * *
##  Aluminum Smelter Credits
Aluminum smelters may qualify for:
  1. a business and occupation (B&O) tax credit for property taxes paid, (credit ID 910) [82.04.4481](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.04.4481)
  2. an exemption from the state portion of retail sales tax and use tax on tangible personal property and all construction at the aluminum smelter, and (credit ID 905) [82.08.805](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.08.805) and [82.12.805](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.12.805)
  3. an exemption from the natural gas use tax.


Persons selling power or gas to aluminum smelters: (credit IDs 890/895)
Qualifying companies selling electricity, natural gas, or manufactured gas to an aluminum smelter may receive a B&O or public utility tax credit provided the selling price is reduced by the amount of the credit. Complete and attach [Credit for Energy Providers to Aluminum Smelters](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/CrdtEnrgyPrvdrsToAlumSmltrs.pdf) (pdf) form to Excise Tax Return. [82.16.0498](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.16.0498); [82.04.4482](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.04.4482)
* * *
##  Bad Debt Tax Credit [801]
Bad debt tax credit is allowed for retail sales tax which has been remitted to the Department, but has become uncollectible and written off for IRS purposes. Completion of a [Schedule B ](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/BadDebtTxCrdt_SchB.pdf)form is necessary only if the sales tax rate at the time of sale is different from the current rate. When the rates are the same, the deduction may be taken on retailing B&O [02] and retail sales [01] tax. [WAC 458-20-196](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/wac/default.aspx?cite=458-20-196)
* * *
##  Capital Gains B&O Tax Credit [997] (Repealed effective Dec. 31, 2025)
This credit is only available for B&O tax paid on the sale or exchange of long-term capital assets that are also subject to Washington’s capital gains tax. The credit is equal to the amount of B&O tax paid on the sale or exchange of the long-term capital asset ([RCW 82.04.4497](https://app.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.04.4497)).
**Note:** This credit is effective January 1, 2022 through December 31, 2025. If you paid B&O tax on sales that qualified for the credit, you may amend the applicable returns.
* * *
##  Clean Alternative Fuel Commercial Vehicle and Vehicle Infrastructure Tax Credit
Businesses are eligible for a business and occupation (B&O) or public utility (PUT) tax credit based on:
  * Purchases of new commercial vehicles and qualifying used commercial vehicles that are principally powered by a clean alternative fuel,
  * Leases of new commercial vehicles that are principally powered by a clean alternative fuel (Effective July 1, 2016), or
  * Costs to modify a commercial vehicle to be principally powered by a clean alternative fuel, including the purchase of tangible personal property incorporated into the vehicle and labor charges.
  * Purchases of alternative fuel vehicle infrastructure component parts, as well as related installation and construction costs.


[Special Notice - Clean alternative fuel commercial vehicles and vehicle infrastructure tax credits expanded](https://dor.wa.gov/forms-publications/publications-subject/special-notices/clean-alternative-fuel-commercial-vehicles-and-vehicle-infrastructure-tax-credits-expanded). This tax preference is subject to public disclosure 24 months after it was claimed. See [Tax Preference Transparency](https://dor.wa.gov/forms-publications/publications-subject/tax-topics/tax-preference-transparency) for more information on this public disclosure.
* * *
##  Commute Trip Reduction Credit [820] (Expired July 1, 2025)
Employers who provide commute trip reduction (CTR) incentives to their employees are eligible for a credit against their B&O tax or public utility tax (PUT) due through June 30, 2025. The accrual period for a property manager that provides incentives to persons employed at a worksite managed by the property manager expired on December 31, 2023.
Applications no longer accepted as of January 31, 2025, and credits cannot be applied to returns filed after June 30, 2025, even if they relate to a prior tax period.
* * *
##  Customized Employee Workforce Training Program [940]
Businesses that participate in the Washington Customized Training Program may take a Business and Occupation (B&O) tax credit for 50% of their payment to the training program. The tax credit may not exceed the B&O tax amount due. No credit can be earned for payments to the program made on or after July 1, 2031. Credits earned in calendar year 2031 may be carried forward and used until December 31, 2032. This program expires July 1, 2033.
See our [Incentives page](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/tax-incentive-programs) for more information about filing requirements. [RCW 82.04.449](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.04.449)
* * *
##  Destination Sourcing Tax Credit [602]
This credit applies only to Washington retail businesses that ship or deliver products they sell to in-state locations.
Beginning July 1, 2008, Washington businesses that ship or deliver goods in-state are required to charge sales tax based on where the customer receives the goods - the destination of the delivery. To help retailers with this change, eligible retail businesses may receive up to $1,000 in tax credits to offset any necessary changes to their accounting system, point of sale, or other systems. Retail businesses are eligible if they meet all of the following requirements:
  * Registered with the Department of Revenue prior to July 1, 2008
  * Physical presence in Washington
  * Gross sales for Washington State is less than $500,000 annually
  * Receive at least 5% of their taxable sales income from deliveries
  * Receive at least 1% of their taxable sales income from deliveries outside the jurisdiction where they collect the most sales tax


How to calculate and report the credit:
  * Calculate total costs incurred one year before or after July 1, 2008, to comply with tax sourcing changes. Costs include goods and services purchased and labor costs.
  * Credit is the lesser of total costs incurred or $1,000. For example, if the total cost incurred was $850, the maximum credit allowed is $850. If the total cost incurred was $1,500, the amount of the credit is limited to $1,000.
  * Credit taken per return cannot exceed the total of B&O taxes plus the state portion of the retail sales tax, minus any other credits. However, any remaining credit may be carried over to the next reporting period until used. 
For example, total costs incurred equal $850. The maximum credit allowed is $850. On the July 2008 tax return, total taxable retail sales equal $8,000.
> State portion of retail sales = $520  
>  B&O taxes = $37.68  
>  Small business B&O credit (SBC) = $35  
>  B&O tax due less SBC = $2.68  
>  B&O taxes due + state portion of retail sales tax = $522.68  
>  Sourcing tax credit allowed on the July 2008 tax return = $522.68
> $327.32 may be carried over to the next reporting period.
  * If at least a portion of the credit is not claimed on a return period within one year after the effective date of July 1, 2008, the credit is no longer available. [RCW 82.32.755](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.32.760)


* * *
##  Employee Ownership Credit [2005]
Approved businesses converting to an employee ownership structure may take a credit from the B&O tax for the costs related to the conversion. An application is required. See the [incentive page](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/tax-incentive-programs) for more information.
Credits can be earned for tax reporting periods starting on or before June 30, 2025. No credits can be claimed for filing periods starting on or after July 1, 2026.
* * *
##  Energy Efficiency Incentive Credit [999]
Effective July 1, 2021, a public utility tax credit is available for qualifying utilities that provide incentive payments to certain owners of qualifying covered commercial buildings or multifamily residential buildings. [Public utility tax credit for payments made to owners meeting the state energy performance standard](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/tax-incentive-programs).
* * *
##  ****Equitable Access to Credit Program - B &O tax Credit
The credit is available to persons that make contributions to the Equitable Access to Credit Program through the Department of Commerce. The credit has an individual cap of $1 million and total statewide cap of $8 million per calendar year and is available on a first-come basis ([RCW 82.04.4499](https://app.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.04.4499); [Tax incentive program – Equitable Access to Credit B&O Tax Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/forms-publications/publications-subject/special-notices/equitable-access-credit-program-bo-tax-credit) ).
* * *
##  External Multiple Activities Credits (MATC) – Taxes Paid to Other States
These credits are allowed for businesses that pay a qualifying gross receipts tax to other states on activities also taxable in Washington. [WAC 458-20-19301](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/wac/default.aspx?cite=458-20-19301); [ETA 3085.2021 – Eligibility of Taxes for Multiple Activities Tax Credits (MATC)](https://taxpedia.dor.wa.gov/documents/current%20eta/3085.2021.pdf).
### Manufactured Outside Washington MATC [67]
The law offers this credit to extractors or manufacturers doing business and paying qualifying gross receipts taxes on their extracting or manufacturing activity. This activity takes place in other states or taxing jurisdictions that are also taxable in Washington.
### Sold Outside Washington MATC [68]
The law offers this credit to extractors or manufacturers doing business and paying qualifying gross receipts taxes on their selling activity in other states or taxing jurisdictions that are also taxable in Washington.  

* * *
## Hazardous Substance Tax [805]
Hazardous substance tax credit is allowed for the tax paid on the value of fuel carried from this state in the fuel tank of airplanes, ships, trucks, or other vehicles. In effect, this gives a tax credit for fuel that was taxed, but not used, in Washington. [WAC 458-20-252](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/wac/default.aspx?cite=458-20-252).
* * *
##  International Services Credit [855] (Repealed Jan. 1, 2026)
This B&O tax credit is available to businesses engaging in certain international services that create and fill new employment positions in Community Empowerment Zones, or contiguous designated census tracts meeting certain unemployment and poverty criteria. The international services must be provided to persons domiciled outside the United States or be for use primarily outside this country. For more information, see our [incentive page](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/tax-incentive-programs#914). [RCW 82.04.44525](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.04.44525).
This credit is repealed effective Jan. 1, 2026. The credit is calculated based on the entire 2026 fiscal year (Jul. 1, 2025-Jun. 30, 2026) but _cannot be claimed after Dec. 31, 2025._
* * *
##  Low-income community solar project cost recovery credit [2003]
Beginning July 1, 2022, light and power businesses are allowed a PUT credit for incentive payments made to low-income community solar projects. Participating community solar projects can begin applying for precertification on July 1, 2022, and must be certified by June 30, 2033.
The maximum annual PUT credit that can be claimed during a fiscal year is 1.5% of your business’s taxable Washington power sales generated in calendar year 2014, or $250,000, whichever is greater.
The right to earn this tax credit expires June 30, 2036. This credit may not be claimed after June 30, 2037.
* * *
##  Main Street Credit [960/961]
Businesses can apply electronically for a credit against the B&O tax and public utility tax equal to 75% of approved contributions made to a Main Street Organization or to the Main Street Trust Fund.
In order to receive a credit, the tax credit must be applied for and approved prior to making a contribution. For more information about the program, visit our [tax incentives page](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/tax-incentive-programs) and [Chapter 82.73 RCW](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/rcw/default.aspx?cite=82.73&full=true).
* * *
##  Manufactured/Sold Inside Washington MATC [69]
The law offers this credit to a business that both extracts and/or manufactures and sells a product at wholesale or retail in Washington.
* * *
##  Motion Picture Competitiveness Program Contributors B&O Credit [950]
Persons who make cash contributions to an approved Motion Picture Competitiveness Program (MPCP) may qualify for a B&O tax credit. MPCP is a nonprofit organization whose sole purpose is to revitalize the state’s economic, cultural, and educational standing in the national and international market of motion picture production. Currently, Washington Filmworks is the only approved organization. The credit has a total statewide annual cap of $15 million and is available on a first-come basis ([RCW 82.04.4489](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/rcw/default.aspx?cite=82.04.4489); [Tax incentive program - Motion Picture Competitiveness Program B&O Tax Credit](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/tax-incentive-programs#921)).
* * *
##  Multiple Activities Tax Credit (MATC) [800]
When a business performs more than one taxable activity for the same product, it reports each activity under the proper classification, but takes the MATC credit so B&O tax is not paid twice on the same amount. For instance, a business that both manufactures and sells a product at wholesale in Washington does not pay both manufacturing and wholesaling B&O tax. A credit is allowed so that B&O tax is paid only once. This also applies to a business that has paid a gross receipt tax to another state. Completion of the [Multiple Activities Tax Credit, Schedule C ](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/MultipleActivitiesTxCrdt_SchC_E.pdf)is necessary each time credit is claimed. [WAC 458-20-19301](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/wac/default.aspx?cite=458-20-19301)
* * *
##  New Employees in Manufacturing and Research & Development in Rural Counties B&O Tax Credit
A credit against B&O taxes is available to businesses that have a business project that is manufacturing or research & development, is located in either a rural county or a Community Empowerment Zone (CEZ) and meets a 15% hiring increase in total employees (at that facility) from the previous four quarters and maintain the new positions for a year.
Applications must be received within 90 days after the first hire date. For more information on the credit, see [Tax credit for new employees in manufacturing and research & development](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-05/NewEmployBOCred.pdf); [Tax incentive program - B&O Tax Credit for new employees in manufacturing and research & development in rural counties](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/tax-incentive-programs#914); [WAC 458-20-240](https://apps.leg.wa.gov/WAC/default.aspx?cite=458-20-240).
* * *
##  Other Credits [810]
_Credit Memorandum:_ If you receive a credit memorandum from the Department of Revenue for previously overpaid taxes, write the credit amount on the Other Credits line of the tax return, and attach the Credit Memorandum.
* * *
##  Pollution Control Credits
The state made a credit available against B&O tax, public utility tax, or use tax for previously paid taxes and/or in lieu of accepting the tax exemptions. These credits are only available to issued certificate holders. We do not allow new applications after 1981.
### B&O tax [805]
The state made a credit available against B&O tax for up to 50 percent of the cost of required pollution control facilities. You may take up to 2 percent of the total credit each year.
### Public utility tax [836]
The state made a credit available against public utility tax for up to 50 percent of the cost of required pollution control facilities. You may take up to 2 percent of the total credit each year.
### Use tax [837]
The state allows a credit against use tax for up to 50 percent of the cost of required pollution control facilities. You may take up to 2 percent of the total credit each year.
* * *
##  Public Utility Tax Credit for Billing Discounts/Qualifying Contributions to a Low Income Home Energy Assistance Fund [880] (Repealed Jan. 1, 2026)
Public Utility Tax credit is allowed for billing discounts and qualifying contributions made by light and power businesses or gas distribution businesses. The credit is itemized on the Credits section of the excise tax return. [Special Notice - Public utility tax credits for billing discounts and qualifying contributions - annual update and notification of repeal.](https://dor.wa.gov/forms-publications/publications-subject/special-notices/public-utility-tax-credit-billing-discounts-and-qualifying-contributions-annual-update-and) For more information, please call [360-705-6218](tel:360-705-6218) or [360-705-6705](tel:360-705-6705).
This credit is repealed effective Jan. 1, 2026. The credit is calculated based on the entire 2026 fiscal year (Jul. 1, 2025-Jun. 30, 2026) but **cannot be claimed after Dec. 31, 2025**.
* * *
##  Renewable energy system cost recovery credit [925]
Light and power businesses can take a public utility tax (PUT) credit for incentive payments to community solar projects (CSPs), shared commercial projects, or renewable energy systems that produce customer-generated electricity.  
  
**Renewable energy system** means a solar energy system, an anaerobic digester, or a wind generator used to produce electricity ([RCW 82.16.110](https://app.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.16.110)). 
The maximum PUT credit during a fiscal year is 1.5% of your business’s taxable Washington power sales generated in calendar year 2014, or $250,000, whichever is greater for incentive payments made for the following:
  * Renewable energy systems that are certified for incentive payment as of June 30, 2020.
  * Community solar and shared commercial projects that are under precertification ([RCW 82.16.165(7)(b)](https://app.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.16.165)) as of June 30, 2020, and that are certified for incentive payment as of June 30, 2022.


The credit may not exceed the tax due.
The right to earn this tax credit expires June 30, 2029. Credits may not be claimed after June 30, 2030.
* * *
##  Sales Tax Paid in Other States [98]
You may take a credit against Washington's use tax for sales or [use tax](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/use-tax) you paid to another state when the property was purchased or first used outside of Washington. [RCW 82.12.035](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/rcw/default.aspx?cite=82.12.035)
* * *
##  Silicon Smelter Credits
Silicon smelters may qualify for an exemption from the brokered natural gas use tax.
Persons selling power or gas to silicon smelters: (credit IDs 892/893)
Qualifying companies selling electricity, natural gas, or manufactured gas to a silicon smelter may receive a B&O or public utility tax credit, as long as the selling price is reduced by the credit amount.
* * *
##  Small Business B&O Tax Credit
Businesses below a certain B&O tax liability are entitled to a credit. The credit varies depending on the total amount of B&O tax due for all classifications after the business takes other available B&O tax credits. There are two credit tables:
### You can take the Small Business Tax Credit [720] if:
  * Your taxable income was**50% or more** reported under Service and Other Activities, Gambling Contests of Chance, For Profit Hospitals, and/or Scientific R&D **and** your:

Filing frequency is: | Total B&O tax liability for filing periods ending before Jan. 1, 2023, is below: | Total B&O tax liability for filing period beginning on or after Jan. 1, 2023, is below:  
---|---|---  
**Filing frequency is:** Monthly |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing periods ending before Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $141 |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing period beginning on or after Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $320  
**Filing frequency is:** Quarterly |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing periods ending before Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $421 |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing period beginning on or after Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $960  
**Filing frequency is:** Annual |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing periods ending before Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $1,681 |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing period beginning on or after Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $3,840  
### You can take the Small Business Tax Credit [815] if:
  * your taxable income was**less than 50%** reported under Service and Other Activities, Gambling Contests of Chance, For Profit Hospitals, and/or Scientific R&D **and** your:

Filing frequency is: | Total B&O tax liability for filing periods ending before Jan. 1, 2023, is below: | Total B&O tax liability for filing period beginning on or after Jan. 1, 2023, is below:  
---|---|---  
**Filing frequency is:** Monthly |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing periods ending before Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $71 |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing period beginning on or after Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $110  
**Filing frequency is:** Quarterly |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing periods ending before Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $211 |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing period beginning on or after Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $330  
**Filing frequency is:** Annual |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing periods ending before Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $841 |  **Total B &O tax liability for filing period beginning on or after Jan. 1, 2023, is below:** $1,320  
When you file [electronically](https://secure.dor.wa.gov/home/Login), our system will automatically calculate your small business credit. The tables are also available on our [Forms page](https://dor.wa.gov/forms-publications/forms-name-s#SBC).
* * *
##  Syrup Tax Credit [945]
Effective July 1, 2006, retailers that pay syrup tax when buying carbonated beverage syrup to make carbonated fountain drinks can claim a B&O tax credit. The portion of the syrup tax allowed as a credit increases each year as follows: July 1, 2006, to June 30, 2007, – 25%; July 1, 2007, to June 30, 2008, – 50%; July 1, 2008, to June 30, 2009, – 75%; After June 30, 2009, – 100%. The credit must be claimed in the tax reporting period in which the syrup was purchased. The B&O tax credit can not be refunded. No credit is allowed for syrup tax paid prior to July 1, 2006. The credit is itemized on the Credits section of the excise tax return. (Substitute Senate Bill 6533, Chapter 245, Laws of 2006) [RCW 82.04.4486](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.04.4486)
* * *
##  Tobacco Products/Cigar Tax Credit [930]
Distributors who first possess tobacco products in the State of Washington are allowed to take credits for:
  * **Interstate and foreign sales** - Available to distributors of tobacco products sold to retailers and wholesalers outside the state for resale. This credit may be taken only for the amount of tobacco products tax reported and previously paid on such products. No credit may be taken for a sale of tobacco products from a stock of goods in this state to a consumer outside the state. See [RCW 82.26.110](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.26.110).
  * **Returned or destroyed goods** - May be taken for tax previously paid when tobacco products are destroyed or returned to the manufacturer. Credits claimed against tax owed or as a refund of tax paid must be supported by documentation.
  * **Sales to the United States Government** - Available to distributors of tobacco products sold to the US Government, or any of its agencies or instrumentalities. This credit may be taken only for the amount of tobacco products tax reported and previously paid on such products.
  * **Sales to Indian Tribal Organizations** - Available to distributors of tobacco products sold to any Indian Tribal Organizations. This credit may be taken only for the amount of tobacco products tax reported and previously paid on such products


Distributors must document the credits. The documentation should conform to requirements outlined in [WAC 458-20-185](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/WAC/default.aspx?cite=458-20-185). For help calculating your credit, use the [Tobacco Products/Cigar Tax Credit Worksheet](https://dor.wa.gov/sites/default/files/2022-02/tobprodcigtxcrwksht_e.pdf) (pdf). The credit is itemized on the Credits section of the excise tax return.
* * *
##  Vapor Products Credit, All Other [993]
Businesses who first possess vapor products that are not accessible containers greater than 5 mL are allowed to take the All Other Vapor Products Credit for vapor products tax previously paid when the products are:
  * Sold and shipped outside Washington
  * Sold to the United States Government
  * Sold to a federally recognized tribe or enrolled tribal member
  * Returned to the manufacturer
  * Destroyed


The credit is claimed on the excise tax return. You must keep documentation to substantiate this credit for five years. No credit is available for vapor products given away for free.
* * *
##  Vapor Solution Credit, Accessible Containers Greater than 5 mL Credit [994]
Businesses who first possess vapor products that are accessible containers greater than 5 mL are allowed to take the Accessible Containers of Vapor Solution Greater than 5 mL Credit for vapor products tax previously paid when the products are:
  * Sold and shipped outside Washington
  * Sold to the United States Government
  * Sold to a federally recognized tribe or enrolled tribal member
  * Returned to the manufacturer
  * Destroyed


The credit is claimed on the excise tax return. You must keep documentation to substantiate this credit for five years. No credit is available for vapor products given away for free.  

* * *
##  Veterans Employer B&O Tax Credit (Effective October 1, 2016, expired July 1, 2023) [970]
A business and occupation (B&O) tax credit is available to businesses that employ an unemployed veteran in a permanent full-time position located in Washington for at least two consecutive full calendar quarters on or after October 1, 2016, and before June 30, 2022.
The credit equals 20 percent of the wages and benefits the business paid to or on behalf of the qualified employee not to exceed $1,500 for that employee. There is no limit on the total credit an employer may receive. However, the total statewide credits may not exceed $500,000 per fiscal year. Credits are available on a first-in-time basis.
Credits are claimed through the Department's E-file system. No application is required. The business must file an Annual Tax Performance Report by May 31 of the year following the year a credit is claimed. [RCW 82.04.4498](http://app.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.04.4498)
* * *
##  Veterans Employer PUT Credit (Effective October 1, 2016, expired July 1, 2023) [971]
A public utility tax (PUT) credit is available to businesses that employ an unemployed veteran in a permanent full-time position located in Washington for at least two consecutive full calendar quarters on or after October 1, 2016, and before June 30, 2022.
The credit equals 20 percent of the wages and benefits the business paid to or on behalf of the qualified employee not to exceed $1,500 for that employee.
There is no limit on the total credit an employer may receive. However, the total statewide credits may not exceed $500,000 per fiscal year. Credits are available on a first-in-time basis.
Credits are claimed through the Department's E-file system. No application is required. The business must file an Annual Tax Performance Report by May 31 of the year following the year a credit is claimed. [RCW 82.16.0499](http://apps.leg.wa.gov/RCW/default.aspx?cite=82.16.0499)

**Warning:** to protect against the possibility of others accessing your confidential information, do not complete these forms on a public workstation.
## Income tax forms
The State of Washington **does not** have a personal or corporate Income Tax. For federal income tax forms, visit the [Internal Revenue Service](https://www.irs.gov/) (IRS).

Print
#  Deductions
We listed each deduction definition below. If you need more help with reporting deductions, [contact us](https://dor.wa.gov/contact).
**Paper filers** : You must attach the Deduction Detail page to any tax return on which you take a deduction. If you do not complete and attach the Deduction Detail pages, we can't accept the information and you may be billed for additional taxes, interest, and penalties.
  * [Advancements/Reimbursements, Returns and Allowances](https://dor.wa.gov/taxes-rates/tax-incentives/deductions#007)
